## VIDEO — 036 — Tell_Me_About_Yourself_Best_Answer_(from_former_CEO)

- **Fichier source** : `Sources/videos/transcripts/TQHW7gGjrCQ_whisper_base_Tell_Me_About_Yourself_Best_Answer_(from_former_CEO).md`
- **URL** : https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TQHW7gGjrCQ
- **Langue Whisper** : `en`

### Transcription (français)

*La piste Whisper n’est pas en français. Verbatim tel quel (souvent anglais) — pour le script oral darija, s’appuyer sur les **Idées clés** ou régénérer / retraduire.*

Hey everyone, so tell me about yourself.

The most common job interview question of all time.

Usually the thing that they ask you first

as an icebreaker when you first sit down

at your job interview.

Now there are a million ways

to answer this open-ended question.

And there's also about a million YouTube videos

out there giving you various ways to answer it.

But today, I'm gonna give you the quickest, simplest,

best way I've seen to answer this question.

Okay, let's look at this thing

from the other side of the fence.

Let's look at it from the perspective

of the recruiter or hiring manager.

Usually when you post the position,

you get a lot of responses

and you may well end up with,

especially these days,

with over 100 candidates applying for the position.

So for you, this is an elimination game.

Your job is to go from 100 applications

down to one candidate that you select.

Now, from the perspective of the job seeker

who's being interviewed,

you don't know the criteria they use

to eliminate people.

Oh, sure, there's posted requirements for the position.

But the problem is more than one person

may meet all posted requirements.

So there's often a hidden criteria

that they don't tell you

of what will get you eliminated or hired.

For example, something I've seen in the past

is a hiring manager who's a fan

of a particular sports team.

And if you happen to volunteer

that you're a fan of the opposing sports team,

that may be grounds to eliminate you

on the fact that you might not be a good fit.

And this does happen.

Now, we're gonna make one assumption here

and that is that they've actually read your resume.

If you apply for a position

and you send in your resume

and then they later receive it

and then call you in for an interview,

usually that means that they've read your resume.

Not always, I have seen cases

where that hasn't actually occurred,

but in the vast majority of cases,

we can assume this to be true.

So what does this mean?

This means that the content on your resume

is safe.

Everything you've written on there

did not result in you getting eliminated.

So it's safe content to use

and we're gonna be coming back to that.

Now, when you get asked, tell me about yourself

in a job interview.

This is what you do.

Start off by saying,

well, as you can see from my resume,

that's the first thing you say.

Then go down your resume in chronological order,

starting with the oldest material

and then getting closer to the present

and finally talking about your most recent experience.

This should take about 45 seconds, no more than a minute.

Then end with the phrase

and that's what brings me here today

and why I'm excited to learn more about this opportunity.

You see, your purpose in a job interview

is to communicate to the person interviewing you,

how you're the person for the job,

how you meet all the qualifications.

That's your purpose in the interview.

You don't want to waste your time talking about something

you did 15 years ago that has absolutely nothing

to do with this position and is just taking up time.

That's why you want to summarize your resume

in 45 seconds to a minute.

No more than that, really.

See, it's a well-known fact that people absorb and retain

only a small proportion of what they hear.

It's like a very small percentage of what you hear

that you actually understand and retain

and can recall later.

So that's why you want to mention more than once

how you meet all the qualifications.

You want to make sure it registers.

So when you get the question, tell me about yourself.

All you have to do is say, well, as you can see

from my resume and then you summarize your resume

in about 45 seconds to a minute.

Maybe start with your education,

start with your oldest experience

and then come up chronologically to the present

where you end with your most recent experience

and then you end with the phrase

and that's what brings me here today

and why I'm excited to learn more about this opportunity.

See, you want to spend as much time as possible

talking about this opportunity,

not stuff you've done in the past.

That's why it's very important to try and steer the conversation

from something you've done years ago

to get them to talk about this position

so you can explain how you meet the requirements.

So this is actually part of a new YouTube series I'm doing.

I'm going to go through all the common job interview questions

and we're going to talk about the hiring process in general.

I actually teach this at a postgraduate level

and I've been on both sides of it, hiring and being hired.

So hopefully that'll be useful for you.

Please take a moment now to click the like,

subscribe, and bell buttons

and also be sure to check out my Patreon site

for some extra content and consider supporting me there too.

So once again, I'm Bill, the company's expert.

Thank you so much for being here

and watching my videos.

You're awesome.


---

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Côté recruteur** : beaucoup de candidats → logique de **filtrage** ; des critères peuvent être **implicites** (ex. affinités) — sensibiliser sans paranoïa.
- **Le CV comme base** : si convocation suite au CV, le contenu du CV est en général **déjà acceptable** ; la réponse peut **s’appuyer dessus** sans tout réinventer.
- **Méthode « Parlez-moi de vous »** : amorce du type **« comme sur mon CV… »**, puis **parcours chronologique** (du plus ancien au plus récent) en **~45 s à 1 min**.
- **Clôture pivot** : phrase du type **« … et c’est ce qui m’amène aujourd’hui ici / sur cette opportunité »** pour **renvoyer au poste** et ouvrir la suite.
- **Redondance utile** : répéter, dans d’autres réponses, **l’adéquation aux exigences** (on retient peu à l’oral) — sans rabâchage mécanique.
- **Économie du temps** : éviter longs détours **sans lien** avec le poste ; **maximiser** le temps sur **l’offre** et les **preuves** d’adéquation.

---

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Public d’origine** : **stage d’observation** de **3e** (France), durée **d’une semaine** — références au **ministère** et au **collège**. Pour **proM7** (**Bac+**, **Maroc**) : **réutiliser** surtout la **structure** du rapport et les **bonnes pratiques** de rédaction ; **longueur**, **grille** et **exigences** = **celles de ton école** / **PFE**, pas celles de la vidéo.
- **Utilité du rapport** : permettre aux **enseignants** de **suivre** l’expérience sans être sur place ; forcer une **réflexion** après coup ; entraîner **rédaction** et **analyse** (compétences **transversales** pro).
- **Plan type** (à adapter) : **introduction** (cadre, dates, lieu) → **sujet** / thème du stage → **présentation de l’organisme** (identité, activité, effectifs, pourquoi ce choix) → **métiers** ou **fiches de poste** observés → **approfondissement** d’**un** poste ou d’**un** sujet qui a particulièrement retenu l’attention → **journal** des **activités** / semaine type → **retour d’expérience** → **conclusion** → **sommaire**, **illustrations**, **annexes**.
- **Fiche de poste** : plusieurs **personnes** peuvent occuper le **même** poste (ex. plusieurs contrôleurs de gestion) — nuance utile pour **PFE** et **veille RH**.
- **Journal de bord** : idéalement **quotidien**, mais **filtrer** pour garder le **fil** du stage ; un **gros** sujet peut faire l’objet d’une **section** à part.
- **Retour d’expérience (« Rex »)** : vocabulaire **pro** ; dire ce qui a **servi** ou **moins servi** avec **arguments** ; pour les points **négatifs**, rester **constructif** et **respectueux** (pas une **chronique** irrespectueuse de l’entreprise).
- **Annexes** : organigramme, **comptes rendus** d’**entretiens**, documents **trop longs** pour le corps du texte — **enrichissent** sans **alourdir** chaque chapitre.
- **Présentation** : traitement de texte, **page de garde**, **sommaire** automatique (styles de titres), **mise en page** lisible — éviter le rendu « **brouillon manuscrit** » pour un document **pro** ou **académique** sérieux.
- **Relecture** : **orthographe**, **clarté** ; si le **cadre** le permet, faire **relire** par le **tuteur** / **maître de stage** pour un **regard extérieur**.
- **Fin de vidéo** : incitation **like / abonnement** — **ne pas** recopier en **script** pédagogique proM7.

**Lien parcours** : **M4** (stage, **PFE**, **rapport**, **soutenance** amont) ; **M0** (méthode, **rédaction**).

---

## VIDEO — 038 — Morocco_Economy_2025_Q2_High_Unemployment_And_Debt_Crisis_Deepens

- **Fichier source** : `Sources/videos/transcripts/u7Y1bhgQxEM_whisper_base_Morocco_Economy_2025_Q2_High_Unemployment_And_Debt_Crisis_Deepens.md`
- **URL** : https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=u7Y1bhgQxEM
- **Langue Whisper** : `en`

### Transcription (français)

*La piste Whisper n’est pas en français. Verbatim tel quel (souvent anglais) — pour le script oral darija, s’appuyer sur les **Idées clés** ou régénérer / retraduire.*

If you're following our global economic outlook series, hit subscribe to stay updated with new

country releases. Morocco economy Q2 high unemployment and debt crisis refers to the persistent challenges

the country faces in stabilizing the labor market and managing rising public debt while attempting

to maintain moderate economic growth. During 2024, 2025, Morocco's GDP annual growth rate

stands at approximately 2.8 percent, reflecting moderate expansion driven by agriculture recovery,

tourism, and service sector performance. However, this growth remains uneven and insufficient to

absorb the labor force entering the job market. The unemployment rate remains high at around 13 percent,

with the problem concentrated especially among youth and urban populations. The interest rate

set by the central bank remains at 3 percent, which aims to balance inflation stability with

limited economic stimulation. The inflation rate is relatively moderate at around 2 percent,

suggesting price pressures have eased compared to previous periods. However, the easing of inflation

has not translated into strong purchasing power recovery as real wages and job opportunities

remain weak. Meanwhile, the debt to GDP ratio is estimated at roughly 69 percent, demonstrating a

growing strain on government finances largely due to borrowing needs for public investment,

social programs, and external economic pressures. In Q2, the high unemployment rate persists as one

of the central economic challenges. The labor market struggles to match job seekers with available

employment, particularly in technical and higher skilled fields. Youth unemployment remains

significantly higher than the national average driven by limited job creation and manufacturing

industry. Many recent graduates face structural barriers, with the economy unable to absorb new

entrance quickly due to slow private sector expansion. The informal sector continues to serve as

a fallback for many workers, but informal work provides unstable income, lacks benefits, and does

not contribute to long-term economic security. The mismatch between educational output and labor

market demand further complicates the situation. As a result, the unemployment problem becomes more

structural than cyclical, requiring reforms in vocational training, industry diversification,

and labor market coordination. The public debt crisis raises additional concerns. The government's

debt to GDP ratio near 69 percent reflects years of accumulated borrowing to support public

infrastructure, subsidies, and social programs. Although the debt level is manageable compared to

some economies, the challenge lies in its pace of increase and the limited fiscal space available

for growth stimulating policies. Servicing public debt occupies a growing share of the government

budget, reducing the ability to invest in job creation, technology upgrades, and targeted economic

incentives. External debt in particular exposes Morocco to fluctuations in global financial conditions,

currency movements, and the cost of international borrowing. Rising global interest rates, heightened

repayment pressures, making it more difficult to roll over or refinance existing obligations

without increasing fiscal vulnerability. Morocco's Q2 economy faces a critical challenge, high

unemployment, and rising public debt. Despite moderate growth and controlled inflation,

let's break down the numbers. GDP growth is moderate at 2.8 percent, driven by recovering agriculture

and tourism. However, this isn't enough to absorb the labor force with unemployment stuck at a

high of 13 percent, especially among the youth. Inflation is controlled at around 2 percent,

but this hasn't translated into relief for households, as real wages remain weak.

Meanwhile, the debt to GDP ratio has climbed to nearly 69 percent straining government finances.

These challenges are interconnected. High unemployment reduces consumer spending,

while high public debt restricts the government's ability to stimulate the economy and create jobs.

Key sectors like tourism and manufacturing show gradual improvement, but expansion remains

insufficient to absorb labor at scale. This creates a cycle of low spending and weak investment,

reinforcing stagnation. The central bank holds interest rates at 3 percent to maintain stability,

but this does little to spur new lending. In summary, Morocco's Q2 situation is defined by this

difficult balancing act. Breaking the cycle requires strengthening productive sectors,

and carefully managing debt while making targeted investments to boost job creation.

As a result, low inflation exists alongside economic hardship for many segments of the

population, highlighting that price stability alone is insufficient to improve overall economic

conditions without stronger employment growth and income support. Government policy during Q2

aims to stabilize finances while responding to social needs. However, balancing fiscal discipline

with job creation efforts remains complex, reducing public spending to aggressively risks worsening

unemployment while increasing spending risk for their expanding public debt. Social protection

programs aim to cushion the poorest households, but these measures alone do not address the structural

shortage of stable job opportunities. Long-term growth depends on improving industrial capacity,

expanding renewable energy sectors, enhancing logistics networks, and deepening trade partnerships.

Yet these initiatives require sustained investment and institutional continuity.

The high unemployment and rising debt pressures also influence investor confidence.

Foreign investors view Morocco as stable relative to some neighboring economies,

but caution persists due to slow labor market absorption and heavy fiscal obligations.

A stable monetary environment supports medium-term planning, yet investment decisions continue

to be influenced by global conditions, tourism demand cycles, and commodity market shifts.

Export growth provides opportunities, but diversification efforts need acceleration to create

resilience against external shocks. Q2 conditions highlight that Morocco's economic challenges

are interconnected. High unemployment reduces consumer spending and tax revenue,

which in turn limits fiscal capacity to reduce debt. High public debt restricts the government's

ability to stimulate the economy, slowing job creation. Moderate growth is insufficient to change

labor market conditions significantly. Stabilizing the economy requires coordinated efforts in

education, labor market training, industrial development, and fiscal reform. In summary,

Morocco's Q2 economic situation is defined by persistent high unemployment and rising debt burdens,

despite moderate GDP growth and controlled inflation. Breaking this cycle requires strengthening

productive sectors, improving workforce skills alignment, and carefully balancing debt management

with targeted economic investment. Morocco economy, Q2 high unemployment and debt crisis refers

to the persistent challenges the country faces in stabilizing the labor market and managing rising

public debt, while attempting to maintain moderate economic growth. During 2024-2025,

Morocco's GDP annual growth rate stands at approximately 2.8%, reflecting moderate expansion driven

by agriculture recovery, tourism, and service sector performance. However, this growth remains uneven

and insufficient to absorb the labor force entering the job market. The unemployment rate remains

high at around 13% with the problem concentrated especially among youth and urban populations.

The interest rate set by the central bank remains at 3%, which aims to balance inflation stability

with limited economic stimulation. The inflation rate is relatively moderate at around 2%,

suggesting price pressures have eased compared to previous periods. However, the easing of inflation

is not translated into strong purchasing power recovery as real wages and job opportunities

remain weak. Meanwhile, the debt to GDP ratio is estimated at roughly 69%, demonstrating a growing

strain on government finances largely due to borrowing needs for public investment, social programs,

and external economic pressures. For more data-driven insights and global market breakdowns,

subscribe and turn on notifications. Stay informed. Stay ahead. This is economics FX,

where clarity meets strategy. Until next time, trade smart.


---

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Lecture « cadre »** : croissance **modérée** peut coexister avec un **marché du travail tendu** si l’**absorption** des entrants et des chercheurs d’emploi reste **insuffisante** — même logique que d’autres sources du dossier (**pas** une fatalité individuelle).
- **Chômage** : la source insiste sur une **surconcentration** chez les **jeunes** et en **milieu urbain** (à **quantifier** avec le **HCP**, pas avec les pourcentages de la vidéo sans recoupement).
- **Inflation maîtrisée ≠ pouvoir d’achat rétabli** : si les **salaires réels** ou les **emplois stables** stagnent, les ménages peuvent rester en **tension** malgré une inflation **plus basse**.
- **Dette publique / PIB** : une **dette élevée** peut **réduire la marge** budgétaire pour investir ou stimuler l’emploi (argument **macro** général) — niveau exact et comparabilité : **sources officielles** uniquement.
- **Taux d’intérêt** : politique monétaire **prudente** (stabiliser les prix) peut **limiter** le crédit bon marché pour les entreprises — lien **indirect** avec **investissement** et **embauche** (schéma simplifié).
- **Secteur informel** : **tampon** d’activité mais **revenus** souvent **irréguliers**, **couverture sociale** faible — enjeu pour parler **stage / CDI / protection** sans moraliser.
- **Décalage formation / emploi** : la source parle de **barrières structurelles** pour les **diplômés récents** et d’un déficit d’**adéquation** — renforce les leçons **compétences**, **alternance**, **veille métier**.
- **Investissement & réputation** : les investisseurs **compareraient** le Maroc à la région mais resteraient **prudents** si l’**emploi** et la **fiscalité** posent question — utile pour expliquer **pourquoi la veille économique** aide à **cibler** les secteurs qui **recrutent**.
- **Pistes évoquées** : formation **professionnelle**, **diversification industrielle**, **énergies renouvelables**, **logistique**, **partenariats commerciaux** — à traduire en **actions concrètes** pour l’étudiant·e (projets, langues, certifications) **sans** promesse d’embauche.

## VIDEO — 039 — How_Recruiters_Use_LinkedIn_In_A_Hidden_Job_Market

- **Fichier source** : `Sources/videos/transcripts/UAb1GKnsr0s_whisper_base_How_Recruiters_Use_LinkedIn_In_A_Hidden_Job_Market.md`
- **URL** : https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UAb1GKnsr0s
- **Langue Whisper** : `en`

### Transcription (français)

*La piste Whisper n’est pas en français. Verbatim tel quel (souvent anglais) — pour le script oral darija, s’appuyer sur les **Idées clés** ou régénérer / retraduire.*

So the first thing that I want to make sure everyone understands is that a crisis actually

creates a hidden job market.

If you haven't been on any of my events recently and don't understand what the term hidden

job market means, let me give you a little backstory on that.

So when you have massive amounts of unemployment, which historically this is the most we've

ever seen, I think in the entire history of the country, and it's sort of long term,

this wasn't people who are hoping this would be sort of a V depression, but it's not.

We know this is going to go on for a long time.

Companies shift gears.

They don't post jobs anymore.

Now, that doesn't mean they're not hiring.

It just means that they're not publicly posting jobs on sites like LinkedIn and Glassdoor

and Indeed and some of these other sites.

When there's low unemployment and companies are having a hard time finding them, they have

to increase their marketing.

So they actually post the jobs on all sorts of different platforms, just hoping that maybe

you will find them.

But now they can't do that.

They physically can't do that.

So what they do is they're still hiring, but they essentially hide the jobs or make them

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Marché « moins annoncé »** : en période de **tension** (chômage, restructurations), certaines entreprises **réduisent** les annonces **grand public** tout en **recrutant encore** — pistes : **page carrières** du site, **veille** ciblée, **réseau**. La narration **US** de la vidéo est **datée** ; le **principe** (moins de visibilité agrégée ≠ zéro embauche) reste **pédagogique** avec **prudence** sur le contexte local.
- **Recruteur chercheur actif** : plutôt que trier des **milliers** de candidatures spontanées, l’orateur décrit un mode où le recruteur **interroge** LinkedIn (outils type **Recruiter**) pour constituer une **liste courte** puis **contacte** quelques profils — intérêt du **profil optimisé** pour la **découvrabilité**, **sans** promesse « ils viendront tous à toi ».
- **Analogie « pages jaunes »** : le profil = **fiche** dans un **annuaire** professionnel ; ce que tu **écris** et **où** tu le places influence les **requêtes** pour lesquelles tu **apparais**.
- **Fonctionnement type moteur de recherche** : beaucoup de profils → la plateforme **classe** selon **pertinence** par rapport aux **filtres** et **mots-clés** du recruteur — renvoie aux bonnes pratiques **titre**, **à propos**, **expériences**, **compétences** (vocabulaire **aligné** sur les postes visés).
- **Test de survol** : une fois dans les résultats, le recruteur **parcourt vite** le profil ; il faut un **premier écran** **clair** (qui je suis, pour quoi je suis pertinent) avant le détail.
- **Juste mesure d’information** : trop **vide** = manque de **crédibilité** ; trop **dense** ou **visuellement chargé** = **fatigue** du lecteur ; viser assez pour **donner envie d’écrire** ou d’appeler, pas tout raconter — proche d’un **message marketing** équilibré.
- **Contenu factuel** : l’orateur insiste sur des **éléments vérifiables** et des **indicateurs** (résultats, périmètre) là où c’est **honnête** — **pas** de chiffres **inventés** pour plaire.
- **Restructuration** : distinction utile entre « **on ne recrute plus** » et « **on recrute autrement** / **autre profil** » après réorganisation — moral : **continuer** la veille et l’**adaptation** du profil, **sans** nier la **concurrence**.

**Lien parcours** : leçons **LinkedIn**, **CV numérique**, **canaux de recrutement** — complète **RQ85sC7rqbI** (marché non annoncé, approche directe) par la **face outil** côté candidat.

## VIDEO — 040 — The_Job_Market_Has_Changed..._Again.

Over just the last six months, the job market has changed dramatically.

Again, back in the good old days of 2024, all workers had to worry about

Wiscoe's jobs, quite firing, job washing, career cushioning, invisible overtime,

application black holes, recentism, digital downsizing, compensation compression,

burnout attrition, and when all else fails, good old-fashioned rolling layoffs.

But today, the job market is dealing with a whole new set of trends.

And don't worry, they come with a whole fresh list of dumb corporate buzzwords.

New economic data, if we are allowed to believe that anymore,

is revealing some stark realities about the ways that people are finding a job,

keeping a job, and progressing in a job.

Unfortunately, as you have probably already guessed, a lot of these changes are

throwing young workers, and in particular, young men out of the frying pan and into the fire.

For the first time ever, unemployment amongst young male college graduates is the same

as non-graduates. The share of unemployed people entering the job market for the first time

is the highest it has been since 1988, and job mobility has effectively frozen.

Now, I know what you might be thinking. All things considered, the unemployment rate still

looks pretty good, right? Well, that might actually be part of the problem.

And if all of this wasn't bad enough already, there is now a good chance that art history majors

are earning more than you are. So ever since you found out about AI, you've learned that your

computer science degree is actually a complete joke. Who college graduates are facing one of the most

challenging markets for entry-level jobs in a decade? It's just like getting the first job

that's so hard. I've tried to apply for jobs for like a year now, and just like most places like

don't get back to me, or they just like say no. I make fun of my college degree all the time,

because I'm not self-conscious. Realize it wasn't worth it, even though society deems it as a great

accomplishment. I'm about to call my school up and say that this degree that I spent four years

trying to get four years was a waste of money. There's a funny but not totally inaccurate anecdote

amongst business analysts. That if you want to find an industry that's about to have really bad

job security, then just look where all the Ivy League grads are going. For a while, that was

oil and gas companies before the 1980s oil crisis. Then it was outsourcing operations before

the Asian financial crisis, then early technology before the dot com crash,

finance before the global financial crisis. And now over the most recent decade,

it's been big tech paying huge salaries to talented graduates early in their careers.

Now obviously there is a lot of hindsight here. Nothing can boom forever. And of course,

a lot of young graduates from top schools are going to try to find a job that pays them as well

as possible, if for no other reason than to start paying back that tuition. The problem is that

everybody else sees these growing industries where people can make good money earlier in their

career, and they try to get qualifications to move into those roles too. But no industry can

boom forever. And by the time most people catch up, they find themselves overqualified for a role

that doesn't exist anymore. For the last 10 years, the story has been that everybody getting laid

off from their factory job should just learn to code. But before that, it was everybody should go

and get an MBA. According to the Graduate Management Admissions Council, 2022, right after the dot

com crash was the all-time peak of people enrolling in postgraduate business school in the hopes that

it would boost their stalling careers. According to the numbers today, it looks like that

well-intentioned but ultimately flawed advice may be going to college at all. As the unemployment

rate is now the same between graduates and non-graduates. After this data went live, there were several

articles concluding that this signifies the end of the higher education payoff which is probably a

bit of an oversimplification for the sake of hyperbole. This is absolutely a concerning trend.

But there are two important details you need to understand about it before you go canceling

that college admission. The first is that if both of these groups have the same rate of unemployment

that doesn't necessarily mean that the earnings advantage of college is gone. Looking for a job

as a qualified engineer is normally going to be better than looking for a job as an unskilled

laborer, so even though the same share of these two groups may be out of work, the earnings of

the college graduates is still higher. Also, something I feel I need to repeat as often as I can,

the unemployment rate is a really narrow statistic that people pay far too much attention to as a

singular data point. To count as unemployed, you need to be out of the job in actively looking for

more work. Today, according to the Bureau of Labor Statistics, about 72 percent of people with

a bachelor's degree or higher qualification are actively working or looking for a job.

That number is falling every year which we will address soon. But it's still significantly higher

than the 56 percent of high school graduates who are actually engaged in the labor force,

and it's even worse for people who didn't graduate high school. But they are getting more involved,

and again we will get to why soon. For now, what you need to remember is that even though this

particular statistic looks bad, and don't get me wrong, it IS bad, we're still more likely to

have a job and have a higher paying job with a college degree. But that's still not the whole

calculation. Degrees are not free, and a lot of people are realizing that lifetime earnings are

great and all, but sometimes a little bit of money early in life with no debt is better than more

money later in life with big repayments the moment you are handed a piece of paper. The trend is that

every year the math is looking a little bit worse, and that is something that should be carefully

considered for any investment with a 40 or 50 year payoff period. But that's just the statistical

details that you need to understand about this graduate unemployment problem. The second and much

more important point is that this only applies to men. The unemployment gap for graduate women

is lower than it has been historically, but it's still pretty wide and it's actually been

growing at the same time the gap for men has been disappearing. And the question is, why?

Well, this strange difference actually reveals a lot about other recent trends in the job market,

so it's time to learn how many works to find out how it's all changing. Again, this week's video

is sponsored by Cape. Cape is a privacy first mobile carrier that gives you premium nationwide

service without tracking your data, selling it, or storing it longer than necessary.

Traditional carriers build profiles on you, who you call, where you are, and what you do.

Cape does none of that. They don't even ask for your name or address to get started,

and what really sets them apart is their cryptographic SIM protection. Your number is secured

with a 24-word recovery phrase, similar to how you'd protect sensitive digital assets.

Honestly, what got me was how they handle SIM swaps. Instead of relying on some call center agent,

Cape gives you full control over your number. If you don't have the key, no one does. No resets,

no override. It's a level of security that finally feels built for how things work today.

And if you're into privacy tools, there's more. Encrypted voicemail, real-time threat

Another subtle, but extremely important change that has been recorded in the job market

is the changing payoff for job hopping. We've mentioned multiple times that workers who are

overly loyal to their company statistically earn significantly less over their working careers

when compared to those who hop jobs for promotions or paybumps. But that has changed. And over

the last year, the benefit has all but disappeared. Now, a little bit of that is because wage growth

is just slowing down overall. But a larger trend is that the job market is encouraging staying

put and doing absolutely nothing. Nobody is hiring. Nobody is leaving their job. Nobody is pushing

for a promotion and nobody is doing anything that could open them up to the next round of layoffs.

According to industry reports, some people are even avoiding new jobs that could be considered

career advancements so they can stay with the company in a role where they are pass probation

and feel less at risk of being let go. This is also benefiting people in less boom and bus

careers like those who went and got an arts degree. Generally, these people go into their fields

because they are genuinely passionate about it over people who are chasing a lucrative career.

They generally take less career risks and hold onto roles that they become extremely

proficient at, which makes them harder to replace than random business and commerce graduate

number A3113. This is not the best strategy in good times if all you care about was making money,

but it gave them a head start on what everybody is doing right now which is holding on to their

job for dear life. This trend of people holding onto the roles has its own buzzword because of

course it has its own buzzword and it's called job hugging. Overall, it's not a great sign when

combined with the less than stellar new jobs data, but it is the logical response by all parties

dealing with increased uncertainty, which is where we get back to this growing gap between young men

and women in the workplace. There is a lot to unpack there, but there are three key differences

driving this trend. The first is the push to equalize gender balance in certain roles,

but not all roles. The push has been toward getting women into male-dominated fields that require

a college degree like STEM and business management, but not as much the unskilled fields that are

also dominated by men like the trades and labor roles. Women in STEM has been a big focus of

government programs, corporate initiatives, and school enrollments for decades at this point,

and it's been highly successful at opening up the field to more talent. This means that men are

competing with a wider base of competition than they would have in the past, and the simple

fact is that there are only so many of these jobs to go around. But at the same time, the men in

roles that don't require a college degree haven't had the same increase in competition. This isn't

a new trend. Before the pandemic shook up a lot of this data, male college grads had an unemployment

rate of around 5%, while their non-graduate peers had an unemployment rate of 6%. Female college

graduates at the same time had an unemployment rate of around 3%. But their non-graduate peers

also had 6% unemployment, so the gap was much wider. Now, it's important to point out that there

have been similar programs to try to get men into historically women-dominated graduate fields too,

especially nursing, age care, and elementary school teaching. But overall, they have been less

successful. Now, there are a few reasons for this. If we are being completely honest with one

another, there is still a stigma around this. A woman landing a role as an engineer or office

executive is seen as empowerment, where a guy becoming a nurse is still the butt of the joke,

and an elementary school teacher is the target of suspicion and raised eyebrows. It absolutely

should not be like this, and it is getting better, but it's silly to pretend it doesn't exist.

The second reason is that historically, these roles have not paid as well, and men have generally

been attracted to more lucrative careers either because they need to support a family,

or simply because that's what they valued. The job market has changed faster than those cultural

expectations, which is why men seek out more typically prestigious jobs. This current gap

is a reflection of that reality. Safe, stable jobs like nursing are doing really well in a bad time

thanks to an aging population, while we are on the tail end of 20 jobs that would have made a lot

of money in a better environment. This also explains why unemployment amongst non-college educated men

has been pretty stable, because construction, the trades, and other semi-skilled jobs have been

pretty stable between increased home construction and infrastructure. You can also see the beating they

took after construction slowdowns from the global financial crisis, which were not nearly as bad for

their college educated peers. Now these differences hurt women in the workforce too.

When women do go into these trendy fields like technology, they actually tend to do worse when

it comes to downsizing. A study on the recent round of tech layoffs sweeping the industry found that

women accounted for 44% of job losses, while only representing 28% of the workforce.

Now, the companies obviously didn't release comprehensive data on why they chose to lay off who,

but generally there are three explanations for this. The first is that these companies may have

hired evenly, but they still segregated genders within different departments,

hiring more women for jobs in HR, marketing, corporate culture, and internal development.

These are, coincidentally, the first departments to get cut downsizing.

The second explanation is that in some ways cultural expectations work for men.

They are seen as a breadwinner supporting a family where the hashtag girl boss is more likely

to lay another feet. This is another example of something that employers should clearly not be doing,

but women are consistently judged more harshly in high performing roles compared to men.

Unfortunately, this often happens particularly from other women, who disproportionately work in

departments like HR which can have a lot of sway over layoff decisions. The third crude explanation

is that hiring practices that targeted a diversity objective over just hiring the best person

for the job favored people who would underperform compared to their peers. So when performance

base layoffs were conducted, these people were more likely to be below the cutoff.

It's no secret that a lot of the cultural forward companies have pulled a hard 180 on a lot of

these initiatives in the last year. Now, I am sure you can probably tell, but I am trying to be

really careful about side-stepping the whole cultural war rabbit hole here, but it's still

important to acknowledge these realities when looking at these issues because even though it shouldn't,

it will have a big impact on everybody's career. One of the best things to do with this

information is to use it to your advantage. Despite the stigma, one of the safest groups from

trouble in the job market are men in previously female dominated fields.

Fields like healthcare already have a low unemployment rate, and men often find it particularly

easy to get these roles because of the practical realities that they can more easily do a lot of

the physical work these roles involve. This was dubbed the Glass Elevator Effect all the way back

in 1992 in a University of Texas article. They found that men often found it much easier to

progress in these roles, and even though initial salaries were lower compared to male dominated

fields, after accounting for the higher chance of career progression, the lifetime earning shifted

back into their favor. Now obviously, don't pick a job because of some video on the internet.

Healthcare in teaching are no joke, but also don't let some business school d***bag talk you out of it,

because chances are you will end up earning more than them. Genuine professions like this are

also more reliant on performance compared to office politics. Go watch this video next to find out

how we forgot what professionalism even means in the modern workplace, and don't forget to like and

subscribe to keep on learning how money works.

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Marché instable** : les **tendances** (secteurs à la mode, types de diplômes valorisés) **changent** dans le temps — le conseil « **tout le monde** doit faire X » (ex. une filière, un métier précis) a souvent **déjà vieilli** quand la masse s’y met.
- **Effet de troupeau** : quand une branche **embauche fort** et paie jeune, beaucoup **s’y précipitent** ; le **ralentissement** peut laisser des profils en **sureffectif** relatif pour des postes qui se **raretient** — argument pour la **veille** et la **différenciation**, pas pour culpabiliser un parcours.
- **Lire les stats avec prudence** : le **taux de chômage** ne raconte qu’une partie de l’histoire (définition du **chercheur d’emploi**, **taux d’activité**, **salaires**, **durée** pour décrocher un premier job, **endettement** étudiant…) — en darija, inviter à **croiser** les indicateurs **sans** importer des chiffres **US** comme vérité locale.
- **Diplôme** : la source argue que **chômage** peut se rapprocher entre groupes tout en restant des **écarts de revenus** — message nuancé : le **diplôme** reste souvent un **actif**, mais le **retour sur investissement** dépend du **domaine**, du **réseau**, du **marché** et du **moment** (aligné proM7 : **pas** de promesse magique).
- **Mobilité professionnelle** : l’idée que « **changer souvent** pour monter en salaire » peut **se tasser** quand le marché **resserre** ; d’autres périodes valorisent la **stabilité** perçue — les deux logiques existent ; l’étudiant·e doit **s’informer** sur son **secteur** au Maroc.
- **Incertitude collective** : comportements de **prudence** (moins bouger, moins viser la promotion « risquée ») peuvent apparaître — à décrire comme **réaction** au contexte, pas comme **fatalité** personnelle.
- **Filières « passion » vs « mode »** : parcours ancrés dans un **métier humain** ou **créatif** peuvent parfois offrir une **stabilité relative** de compétences **difficiles à remplacer** par rapport à des rôles **standardisés** — **très** dépendant du contexte ; éviter les généralisations du type « l’art history bat l’info » (boutade de la source).
- **Stéréotypes de métier** : la vidéo évoque **stigmates** autour de certains métiers **genrés** et des **biais** en entreprise — utile pour un module **égalité / choix de carrière** **si** traité avec **recul** et **exemples marocains** (sans importer la polémique anglo-saxonne telle quelle).
- **À exclure ou reprendre avec un juriste / des sources MA** : interprétations sur **licenciements**, **diversité**, « **glass elevator** », etc. — trop **chargées** pour une leçon emploi **sans** cadrage et **sans** données locales.

in the UK and also served as an advisor to the Department of Education in the country.

My first question for you is what do your experiences tell you about soft skills?

Education now is far more tuned into the needs for children to not only understand the

world that they live in now, but also be able to cope with the world that they're going

Do you tell me a little more about that? Of course, yeah. Every single Nordanglia child

gets an opportunity to work within a Juilliard supported curriculum. So Juilliard support

as in writing the curriculum. They train our teachers within drama music, dance, and

that enables us to teach in a very sophisticated way. So that's Juilliard. MIT, we set a series

of challenges within MIT. Again, we work very collaboratively with the team in Boston.

We can actually go and be in MIT. We have trips each year to both Juilliard and MIT. Our staff

go to MIT for their training. Being part of that as a teacher and being trained and developed

by the MIT is very, very important. I know that to Nordanglia has 82 schools across 33

countries in the world. What are the advantages of being in the network of international schools?

So we can have children from Boston, from the Dominican Republic, from Madrid, Budapest,

and from Hong Kong, all collaborated together on a single project. We compete in sport,

both remotely and face-to-face. Football teams, basketball teams, volleyball, we're just

organizing for the autumn of next year to do a China region sports challenges. And my last

question for you, why is it so important to start this approach young? The quicker they can do

that, the more adaptable they will be. The more adaptable they will be, the easier they will be

to call in those situations, however they come at them. And to be able to recognise those

inherent skills that they are beginning to build up that will help them in the future.

Thank you very much for coming to the S&P Studio today Kenny.

Thank you and it's been lovely to have this opportunity to speak to you.

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Double horizon** : l’éducation vise à comprendre le **monde actuel** et à **tenir** face au **monde à venir** — les soft skills y sont présentées comme **boussole** (résilience, curiosité, confiance, aisance avec soi, empathie).
- **Résilience ≠ brutalité** : développer résilience et confiance via des **situations encadrées** (« contrôlées »), pas seulement par la **pression** ou les épreuves « à tout casser » — angle pédagogique transposable (projets, jeux de rôle, debriefs).
- **Définir le succès** : idée de **succès personnel** (plusieurs voies) et de **réduction des obstacles** plutôt qu’une seule grille — utile pour parler aux étudiant·e·s marocain·e·s sans **uniformiser** les parcours (avec réalisme marché).
- **Équilibre** : **socle académique large** + **développement des soft skills** en parallèle — message « les deux se nourrissent » (pas opposition binaire).
- **Arts / sciences / défis** : la source met en avant **partenariats** (ex. arts scéniques, défis type « lab ») pour **complexifier** l’apprentissage, la **collaboration** et l’**exigence** — équivalents possibles : labs école, associations, hackathons, événements inter-écoles.
- **Réseau & diversité** : **projets à distance** entre profils et lieux différents → **adaptabilité**, travail en **équipe distribuée** — compétence de plus en plus mentionnée en entreprise (à illustrer avec exemples **locaux** en darija).
- **Commencer tôt** : plus tôt on **entraîne** curiosité, confiance et adaptation, plus il est **facile de s’ajuster** quand les situations changent (premier stage, première équipe, premier client) — lien direct avec **parcours stage & emploi**.

Je rappelle qu'on stage si une période durant laquelle un étudiant vient en quelque sorte

découvrir la vie professionnelle au sein d'autant d'entreprise pour mettre en pratique

ses connaissances théoriques et développer ses compétences.

Ce qu'il faut bien noter c'est que cette expérience-là elle doit être formalisée par

une convention de stage qui est très partie de, c'est-à-dire qu'elle est entre ton

entreprise, l'établissement d'enseignement et le stageur lui-même.

Et c'est le code de l'éducation et non le code du travail qui n'est pas à régir en quelque

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Titre** « guide **complet** » : **décalage** avec un **Short** de quelques secondes — ne garder que l’**idée centrale**, pas le **marketing** du titre.
- **Stage** (rappel) : période pour **découvrir** le travail réel, **appliquer** les savoirs **académiques** et **développer** des **compétences** — objectif **pédagogique** et **professionnalisant**.
- **Convention de stage** : acte **tripartite** impliquant en principe **l’établissement d’enseignement**, **l’organisme d’accueil** et le **stagiaire** — formalise **durée**, **cadre**, **responsabilités** (détail selon **textes** applicables).
- **Cadre juridique** : l’exposé oppose **code de l’éducation** (ou équivalent) et **code du travail** « salarié classique » — logique **souvent française** dans ce type de contenu ; pour **proM7** (public **Maroc**) : **recouper** avec les **règles locales** des **conventions de stage** / **stages obligatoires** (établissement, **assurance**, **gratification** si due, etc.) — **ne pas** recopier un **schéma FR** sans **vérification**.
- **Côté accueil** (entreprise) : prévoir **intégration**, **tuteur** / **référent**, **missions** cohérentes avec la **formation** — aligné avec les bonnes pratiques **RH** même si la vidéo ne les développe pas.
- **Côté stagiaire** : **lire** et **comprendre** la convention **avant** signature ; en cas de doute, **école** ou **service** compétent.

**Lien parcours** : **M4** (stage) ; complément **juridique** avec sources **MA** et fiches **école**.

### Idées clés (proM7)

**À recycler avec prudence** — le fond de l’émission mélange **outils de planification** et **discours inspirant** parfois **trompeur** sur la causalité (succès attribué rétrospectivement au tableau).

- **Définition utile (recadrée)** : « savoir **ce qu’on veut vraiment** » + enchaîner avec des **gestes concrets** qui rapprochent du but — **pas** l’idée qu’il suffit de **souhaiter** depuis le canapé.
- **Vision board → tableau d’actions** : un support visuel peut aider à **clarifier** priorités (emploi, mobilité, compétences) à condition d’y associer **étapes**, **dates** et **indicateurs** — sinon risque de **passivité**.
- **Abondance / risque** (version proM7) : distinguer **prudence légitime** et **évitement** systématique ; **oser** des démarches **mesurées** (candidature, réseau) **sans** promettre que « le cerveau cessera d’avoir peur ».
- **Désir « magnétique »** : vérifier que l’objectif vient de **soi**, pas de la **comparaison** (mariage, startup, « comme les autres sur LinkedIn ») — alignement avec **parcours perso** et marché **réel**.
- **Patience** : changer d’habitudes ou de compétences prend du temps ; **persévérance** et **itération** plutôt que abandon au premier refus — **sans** lier ça à une « reconnexion universelle ».
- **Harmonie / connexion** : l’invitée dit ne pas vouloir réussir **au détriment** d’autrui — transposable en **déontologie** pro (concurrence loyale, honnêteté en entretien).
- **Auto-observation comportementale** : repérer où l’on **ferme** une porte (ignorer un contact, ne pas relancer, éviter l’oral) et décider d’un **petit ajustement** la prochaine fois — méthode **concrète**, indépendante du vocabulaire « manifestation ».
- **Gratitude / routine** : une **routine** matinale (respiration, noter une chose positive) peut aider l’**humeur** et la **régulation** — en leçon : **optionnel**, **pas** de garantie sur les **hormones** ni sur les résultats professionnels.
- **Affirmations visibles** : rappels positifs dans l’environnement — **utile** si les messages restent **crédibles** et **actionnables** ; **contre-productif** si ça remplace les **preuves** (CV, projets, entraînement).
- **Espace pour l’imprévu** : laisser de la **flexibilité** dans le plan (rencontres, opportunités non prévues) tout en **poursuivant** les actions — **pas** la même chose que « laisser faire le hasard » sans effort.

**Lien parcours** : **objectifs de recherche emploi / stage**, **plan hebdo**, **réseau**, **résilience** aux refus — en **darija** : insister sur **travail + méthode**, **pas** sur la **loi d’attraction** ni sur des **garanties**.

---

## VIDEO — 044 — The_invisible_rules_of_starting_your_first_corporate_job

- **Fichier source** : `Sources/videos/transcripts/x3JTTU6vHHE_whisper_base_The_invisible_rules_of_starting_your_first_corporate_job.md`
- **URL** : https://www.youtube.com/shorts/x3JTTU6vHHE
- **Langue Whisper** : `en`

### Transcription (français)

*La piste Whisper n’est pas en français. Verbatim tel quel (souvent anglais) — pour le script oral darija, s’appuyer sur les **Idées clés** ou régénérer / retraduire.*

Visible rules of starting your first corporate job. When you get an assignment,

you should always explain back the instructions to the person giving them to you.

It'll help you understand the assignment better and also ensure that they

explain it correctly. And in general, you should just write everything down, including

assignment details. Not only is it helpful for memory, but it's also helpful for CYA.

Next, develop an email filing system, a lot of your job in a corporate context is honestly

finding emails on the social front, prioritize finding trusted mentors. They will be the ones

to help guide you through any particular, like, corporate situation you might have.

And when in doubt, ask the EAs, they know all. Managing upwards will make your life

infinitely easier and also help make sure that you don't cancel things because of work.

And then on the financial front, max out your retirement contributions and save

six, 12 months of an emergency fund as soon as possible. If you're hoping to save

up to become an artist or something, maybe save up even like two years of emergency funds.

Lastly, try to stay for at least a year. It just looks better.


---

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Reformulation des consignes** : après une consigne, **reformuler** ce que tu as compris (objectif, délai, livrable) — limite les **malentendus** et montre le **sérieux** ; complété par **prise de notes** (détail des tâches) pour **mémoire** et **traçabilité** si le périmètre bouge.
- **Organisation mail / fichiers** : en entreprise, une part du temps est **retrouver** l’info (échanges, pièces jointes) — mettre en place tôt un **classement** simple (dossiers, règles, recherche) ; utile **stage** et **premier job**.
- **Mentorat de confiance** : identifier une ou deux personnes **expérimentées** (pas seulement le « copain de open space ») pour **décoder** les **codes** du lieu ; **sans** remplacer le **tuteur** / **manager** officiel.
- **Assistants de direction / bureau** : souvent **nœuds d’information** (calendriers, procédures) — **respect** et **politesse** ; transposable aux **assistantes** / **office managers** dans les structures MA.
- **Managing up** : anticiper les **attentes** du manager (points réguliers, **bad news** tôt), **clarifier** les priorités — réduit les **frictions** ; nuancer « **infinitely easier** » : c’est un **levier**, pas une **magie**.
- **Finances** : version US (**retraite**, **fonds d’urgence** 6–12 mois) — en leçon MA : parler d’**épargne de précaution** et de **stabilité** sans imposer des **montants** US ; **pas** de conseil **fiscal / placement** détaillé hors périmètre proM7.
- **Durée minimale** : « **rester au moins un an** » pour l’**image** sur le CV — **discuter** : **stage** = durée **contractuelle** ; premier CDI = **prudence** avant de **démissionner** sans projet, mais **pas** culpabiliser les **contrats courts** **subis** (précarité, boîte qui ferme).

**Lien parcours** : **entrée en entreprise**, **premier stage**, **soft skills** opérationnels — format **court** : peut servir de **checklist** en darija, avec **filtre culturel** Maroc.

---

## VIDEO — 045 — What_is_a_Company

- **Fichier source** : `Sources/videos/transcripts/XmHk7pNQ79s_whisper_base_What_is_a_Company.md`
- **URL** : https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XmHk7pNQ79s
- **Langue Whisper** : `en`

### Transcription (français)

*La piste Whisper n’est pas en français. Verbatim tel quel (souvent anglais) — pour le script oral darija, s’appuyer sur les **Idées clés** ou régénérer / retraduire.*

What is a company? A company is a legal entity that people form.

It allows them, usually as shareholders, to buy and sell goods and services.

Most companies want to make a profit. They are profit-making entities.

However, some companies are non-profit organisations. They do not make a profit.

Just like humans, companies can hire and fire workers.

Companies can also buy shares in other companies, sue and be the target of a lawsuit.

Additionally, companies can borrow and lend money and own properties.

For example, the image on the left shows that ACME Limited has borrowed $10 million from the bank.

It's lent John Doe $1 million and the company owns 11 golf courses.

What's the difference between a company, a firm and a corporation?

The word company firm and corporation often have the same meaning, but not always.

If you own a business that employs 30 workers, you own a company or firm, but not a corporation.

We refer to a partnership of accountants or lawyers, typically as a firm, we don't usually call it a company or corporation.

There are thousands of types of companies around the world.

Some, such as public limited companies, have shares that investors buy and sell on a stock exchange.

With private limited companies on the other hand, shares only change hands through private arrangement.

Thank you for watching this market's business news video on companies.


---

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Personne morale** : une **société / company** est une **entité juridique** distincte des personnes physiques — elle peut **agir** au nom propre (contrats, dettes, biens) selon le droit applicable.
- **Actionnaires** : souvent les **détenteurs de parts** ; objectif fréquent : activité **économique** (vente de biens / services) avec **lucrativité** ; à distinguer des structures **sans but lucratif** (ONG, certaines associations — logique différente).
- **Capacités typiques** (schéma pédagogique) : **embaucher / licencier**, détenir des **parts d’autres entités**, être **partie** à un litige, **emprunter / prêter**, **posséder** des actifs (locaux, équipement…).
- **Vocabulaire anglais** : *company*, *firm*, *corporation* se **recouvrent** souvent mais pas toujours — ex. cabinet d’**experts** (avocats, comptables) souvent appelé **firm** ; **corporation** évoque plutôt une forme **capitaliste structurée** / cotée selon les pays.
- **Public vs privé (actions)** : société **publique** (côtée) = parts échangées sur un **marché réglementé** ; **privée** = transfert de parts plutôt **négocié entre parties** — utile pour comprendre **qui possède** l’employeur lors d’une veille (sans entrer en droit des valeurs).
- **Lien parcours** : aider l’étudiant·e à lire une **fiche entreprise** ou un **communiqué** (« filiale », « holding », « levée de fonds ») en comprenant que derrière il y a une **structure juridique** et des **intérêts** — **pas** une « personne » unique comme un prof.

---

## VIDEO — 046 — La_personnalité_de_l'entreprise

- **Fichier source** : `Sources/videos/transcripts/y-LA4PRiTeA_whisper_base_La_personnalité_de_l'entreprise.md`
- **URL** : https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y-LA4PRiTeA
- **Langue Whisper** : `fr`

### Transcription (français)

Bonjour, je suis Samuina Jeffal, coach professionnel, certifié à Chez Paris, et

analyse-te-trossactionnel, certifié par le ATA et docteur en économie.

Chaque semaine, je vous partage un concept pour éclairer un sujet d'actualité.

L'objectif étant d'aider à prendre du recul sur ce sujet, alors n'hésitez pas à

partager, liker et à vous abonner si vous souhaitez être tenu informé.

Aujourd'hui, je vous parle de la personnalité de l'entreprise.

La personnalité de l'entreprise, c'est celle qui fait la différence avec les trois

autres composantes du business modèle dans le jeu conclantiel. La personnalité de l'entreprise

est ce qui allait ment à la fois les énergies individuelles et les énergies collectives.

C'est ce qui donne envie de faire, de réaliser comme de faire partie. Cette personnalité pourrait se

définir en trois éléments empilables. Le premier élément, si tu es juste en bas ici, c'est la

raison d'être de l'entreprise. Cette raison d'être, c'est ce qui explique que cette construction

anthropologique, qu'elle entreprise, lui donne du sens, c'est ce qui explique qu'elle existe,

qu'elle est là pour faire quelque chose au sein de la société dans lequel elle est romaine.

A quoi ce groupe qu'elle entreprise, c'est être vivant, certes-il, qu'elle est sur l'utilité

dans la société, dans son économie. Est-ce que ce groupe, ce collectif répond bien à des

sollicitations exprimées ou latentes de l'environnement ? Qu'est-ce qui fait que des individus se reconnaissent

dans cette utilité et acceptent voir des ires participer à cette aventure ? Là et la raison d'être,

le commun qui va faire socle pour l'énergie individuelle qui rencontre l'énergie collective pour faire

ensemble quelque chose. Le deuxième élément est la culture de l'entreprise. Cette culture, c'est ce

qui fait que le collectif offre à ces différentes parties prenantes, notamment au collaborateur,

un environnement de coopération compatible avec les aspirations individuelles. En quoi cette

organisation représente-t-elle un avantage pour moi ? Ça gite-il là d'une société dans laquelle

je vais pouvoir vivre professionnellement, m'y épanouir, m'enrichir et enrichir mon expérience,

tout en voyant, mes apports reconnus. La troisième dimension de cette personnalité de l'entreprise et

l'ambition de l'entreprise ou son aspiration. C'est ce qui fait qu'il y a des objectifs imaginés en

commun des rêves que l'on pense atteignable ensemble. C'est ce qui fait que ce collectif a envie de

bouger, ça peut être pour un temps, un an, trois ans, cinq ans ou plus longtemps. Comme tout

être vivant, l'entreprise a une personnalité. Cette dernière va évoluer au grail des modifications

de l'environnement. Elle est, comme vous le voyez dans ce schéma, le soubassement du business model,

soubassement souvent, on va dire invisible, implicite, qui va faire que le business model va bouger en

phase avec son environnement et sera capable même de se transformer. Le business model est en ces trois

composants de du haut qui sont la proposition de valeur au sommet du triangle, ce que les parties

prennent à chat ou exige, ce qu'elles attendent de l'entreprise. L'architecture de valeur, c'est-à-dire

comment l'entreprise s'organise, qu'elle partenaire à le choisir, ses processus clés, ses savoirs faire et puis comment l'entreprise crée de la

richesse en faisant ça. Car, elle en a besoin pour survivre. Ce n'est pas un but en soi. Il s'agit pour l'entreprise de continuer à

créer de la valeur et pourquoi elle est effectivement rémunérée. Voilà pour aujourd'hui, j'espère que ce

concept et ce schéma vous sera utile pour décoder une situation que vous pouvez être en train de vivre,

car je trouve qu'aujourd'hui, la question de la quête de sens souvent posée par les salariés,

même, est une question qui, en réalité, vient nous parler de ces trois éléments fondamentaux où la

personne rencontre aussi l'entreprise et s'est investi pleinement. Je vous remercie et à bientôt.


---

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Personnalité de l’entreprise** (concept présenté) : ce qui **sous-tend** le **business model** — souvent **implicite** — et **aligne** les **motivations individuelles** avec l’**élan collectif** (envie d’agir, de contribuer, d’**appartenir**).
- **Trois « blocs » empilables** : (1) **raison d’être** — utilité pour la **société** / l’**économie**, réponse à des besoins **exprimés ou latents** ; ce qui fait que des personnes **adhèrent** au projet ; (2) **culture** — cadre de **coopération** pour les **parties prenantes** (dont les collaborateurs) : « **qu’est-ce que cette organisation m’apporte** » (épanouissement, **reconnaissance** des apports, expérience) ; (3) **ambition / aspiration** — **objectifs** et **horizons** partagés (ex. 1 à 5 ans ou plus), envie de **bouger ensemble**.
- **Triangle du business model** (schéma évoqué) : en **sommet**, la **proposition de valeur** (ce que les parties prenantes **attendent** / **exigent**) ; **architecture de valeur** — **organisation**, **partenaires**, **processus**, **savoir-faire** ; **richesse** créée comme **condition de survie** et de poursuite de l’activité — **pas** présentée ici comme une **fin en soi**.
- **Évolution** : comme un « être vivant », la personnalité **change** avec l’**environnement** — le business model peut **s’ajuster** ou se **transformer** en cohérence avec ce socle.
- **Quête de sens** (jeunes / salariés) : question utile en **entretien** et **choix d’employeur** — croiser **ses propres attentes** avec **raison d’être, culture et ambition** de la structure (sans romantisme : **contrats** et **réalités** du marché restent à cadrer proM7).
- **Transcription** : noms / sigles **approximatifs** (Whisper) — **ne pas** les **citer** comme **sources officielles** dans un script ; garder les **notions**.

**Lien parcours** : **M2** (comprendre l’entreprise, business model) ; **M4–M5** (veille employeur, **culture**, pourquoi cette boîte) ; **M6** (image pro, adéquation valeurs / projet).

---

## VIDEO — 047 — FIND_JOBS_in_MOROCCO_-_the_Mindset_you_NEED

- **Fichier source** : `Sources/videos/transcripts/YI_RRKR2zaI_whisper_base_FIND_JOBS_in_MOROCCO_-_the_Mindset_you_NEED.md`
- **URL** : https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YI_RRKR2zaI
- **Langue Whisper** : `en`

### Transcription (français)

*La piste Whisper n’est pas en français. Verbatim tel quel (souvent anglais) — pour le script oral darija, s’appuyer sur les **Idées clés** ou régénérer / retraduire.*

Hello Morocco, are you looking for a job or do you know somebody who's searching for

work?

Today we're going to talk about the proper mindset during a job search.

Let's do it.

I want to share three tips about your mindset, your perspective that will help you well looking

for work.

Number one, no one owes you a job.

You don't deserve a job.

You are not entitled to a job.

Businesses don't hire people as an act of charity.

They exist to make money for the owner or the shareholders.

And so they're not giving you a job to try to help you out.

They're giving you a job to help themselves out.

So when you go to find a job, you don't need to convince somebody to help you.

You have to convince somebody that you can help them, that you can benefit them.

Get it out of your head, that the world owes you a favor.

Even if you've studied hard and graduated, even if you've got your degree, you have a

master's, you have a PhD, the world still does not owe you a job.

Don't be surprised.

Don't be shocked if the picture you posted on Facebook of your graduation picture with

your cap and your gown didn't result in companies calling you up and inviting you to

come and work for them.

The world doesn't owe you a favor.

It doesn't work like that.

Secondly, I often hear from Moroccans how hard it is to find a job here.

I agree with you.

It is hard to find jobs here in Morocco.

I've seen the unemployment statistics.

I see the World Bank giving money to Morocco to stimulate the economy, to try to kickstart

things, to improve the job situation here.

It is hard to find a job here.

That's the situation we're in.

But here's the thing.

You don't control the situation.

You control your response to the situation.

So except that it's hard, then go out and crush it.

Sitting at the cafe, complaining that there's no jobs, going to government protests and

demanding that they solve your problems, or envying people who have money or connections

or a foreign passport, it doesn't help you in any way.

Being sorry for yourself, complaining or pouting doesn't change anything.

Yes, it's difficult.

It's hard to find a job.

Except that and go out and crush it.

Now if something's difficult, it doesn't mean that it's impossible.

If 20% of young educated Moroccans cannot find a job, that means 80% can.

80% do have jobs.

So why are you among the 20%?

What would it take for you to be among the majority who do find work?

What will it take for you to overcome this challenge?

The third mindset you need during the job search is that it's all about offering value.

So if businesses don't give money to their employees as charity, why do they pay people?

It's because it will benefit them.

Because their employees are offering value to the owners or the shareholders of the company.

So if you can bring value, if you can offer something, if you can contribute more than

you're taking, if you can help the company make more money than they're paying you, then

you're offering value.

Try to see things from the employer's perspective.

Try to put yourself in their shoes.

Why should they hire you?

What are you offering them?

Are you bringing to the company?

Do you have any skills?

Do you have any qualifications?

Do you have any useful knowledge?

Do you have experience?

And if you answer no to these things, then you need to hustle.

You need to demonstrate to the employer that you will work harder and learn faster than

all the other people that are competing for that same job.

Now there's a university in Casablanca that I'd like to teach at.

I've got my MBA, I've got years of experience teaching, and I'm the only person qualified

to teach the course I'm offering in all of North Africa.

I bring a lot of value, I'm offering a lot of value to the university.

But still, I've visited the campus six times in person over the last ten months.

Even though I can offer value, it still takes hustle.

So if you're looking for a job in Morocco, make sure you've got the right mindset.

Make sure you've got the right perspective.

No one owes you a job.

Yes, it's hard to find work, but you need to accept that and then go out and crush it.

And you need to bring value to a company.

If you don't have much to offer, then you need to hustle.

Okay, remember this, this little expression.

If it has to be, it's up to me.

It is your life.

It is your responsibility to find a job.

It's not your parents' responsibility, it's not the government's responsibility, it's

not your family member who lives overseas responsibility, it's up to you.

If it's got to be, it's up to me.

What do you think?

Do you have any other tips for a healthy mindset while searching for a job?

Let me know in the comments below.

And also like, subscribe, and if you have a friend who's looking for a job that could

benefit from this video, be sure to share it with them.

It could help them shift their perspective and make a big difference.

Until next time, get wisdom.

### Idées clés (proM7)

- **Logique employeur** : une entreprise embauche en général pour **résoudre un problème** ou **générer plus de valeur** que le coût du poste — le message utile pour l’étudiant·e : « **qu’est-ce que j’apporte à l’organisation ?** », pas seulement « **aidez-moi** ».
- **Diplôme ≠ file d’attente** : le parcours académique est un **atout**, pas une **créance** automatique sur un emploi — caler avec la règle proM7 (**pas** de promesse de débouchés).
- **Difficulté du marché marocain** : la source **reconnaît** un contexte **dur** — utile pour **normaliser** la recherche sans **fataliser** : l’enjeu est **d’agir** avec **méthode** (candidatures, compétences, réseau, stages).
- **Agir sur son périmètre** : investir son énergie dans des **actions** (formation, preuves, entretiens) plutôt que dans la **rumination** seule — **sans** nier les **obstacles structurels** (réseau, genre, territoire, secteur) : en darija, **équilibre** entre **agentivité** et **réalisme**.
- **Proposition de valeur** : lister **compétences**, **projets**, **langues**, **expériences** ; si le carnet est **mince**, la source parle de **compensation** par **effort**, **curiosité**, **vitesse d’apprentissage** — à formuler sans **sur-travail** ni **burnout** comme norme.
- **Persévérance** : l’exemple des **multiples démarches** sur place pour un objectif pro — illustre la **régularité** et le **suivi** (adaptable : relances, visites, salons, LinkedIn).
- **À ne pas reprendre tel quel** : la **statistique** « 20 % / 80 % » (jeunes diplômés) — **absente de source** dans la vidéo ; les **généralisations** sur ce que « les Marocains » font au café ou en politique — **stigmatisantes** et hors rôle pédagogique proM7.
- **Slogan « if it has to be, it’s up to me »** : rappel de **responsabilité personnelle** — utile si **couplé** à des **ressources** (accompagnement école, proM7, pairs) et **jamais** pour **isoler** la personne ou **nier** le besoin d’**aide**.

- **Langue Whisper** : `fr`

### Transcription (français)

Coach Edemisile, le conseil bien-être de nos experts.

Bonjour, je suis Éle Dignel Zarek, je suis semiologue et je viens de sortir un ouvrage

la stratégie du Caméléon, dans lequel j'aborde la question notamment de la personnalité

et de la gestion de ces personnalités.

En la matière, c'est vrai que l'hyper dominant ou l'hyper conquérant

et bien c'est souvent la personnalité qui pose le plus de problème

en tous les cas, ça correspond à la majorité des témoignages que j'ai recueilli.

A moi j'ai quelques astuces à vous donner trois pour justement pouvoir gérer

ce type de personnalité qui veut souvent vous forcer à faire ce que vous avez pas envie de faire.

Alors on pourrait prendre par exemple un boss qui vous dit le vendredi à 17h

qui faut absolument rester pour travailler sur un projet tout weekend

alors que vous avez prévu autre chose le week-end.

Donc la première astuce surtout, je sais que c'est pas facile,

mais il faut s'y tenir, on ne se justifie pas.

C'est-à-dire qu'à partir du moment où vous commencez à rentrer dans une gestification

de non je ne peux pas car ce week-end j'ai prévu, tata-tata,

non je ne peux pas parce que je dois garder mes enfants,

non je ne peux pas parce que j'ai l'anniversaire d'un ami, etc.

Ça y est, vous avez perdu parce que plus vous donnez de la gestification

plus c'est de la matière pour le dominant et le concurrent.

Donc en définitive vous le faites qu'apporter de l'eau à son moulin.

Donc surtout on ne se justifie pas.

Deuxième astuce justement, on regarde la personne avec des yeux de poisson mort.

C'est-à-dire que la personne elle va arriver généralement en hyper concurrence.

Donc à ces dynamiques à vous voir imposer son point de vue.

Et bien là on va regarder de manière très neutre.

Alors quand je dis avec des yeux de poisson mort, ça veut dire en fixant la personne

et non pas avec le menton relevé qui peut être pris comme du défi.

Ou même en souriant ça peut être aussi pris comme du défi.

Donc la personne elle pourrait le prendre personnellement.

Donc on regarde de manière la plus neutre possible avec des yeux de poisson mort.

C'est-à-dire que dans sa tête on pense à autre chose.

Et on peut même s'amuser à compter.

A compter par exemple de 1 jusqu'à 10 alors ça peut être très long.

Mais c'est un petit peu le but recherché parce que les dominants et les concurrents

ils sont très mal à l'aise avec les silences.

Parce que eux, plus vous leur donnez de la matière c'est ce qu'on a vu.

Plus voilà ça apporte de l'eau à leur moulin.

Mais si il y a plus d'eau au moulin, il soit un petit peu gêné et forcément

ils sont obligés de descendre la température et ils sont plus dans le show.

Il y a quelque chose qui est pour eux vient un peu réiller la machine.

Donc vraiment on regarde de manière la plus neutre possible.

On ne pense rien.

Quitte à l'écrire sur un papier si il s'agit d'un entretien téléphonique

et qu'on est au téléphone avec la personne.

Quitte à l'avoir écrit dans la pomme de sa main.

Si jamais c'est un entretien de visu et qu'on a peur de perdre le fil.

Et ça c'est vraiment très important parce que le concurrent,

il va vous amener très facilement et très vite avec lui.

Donc il faut rester ferme et par contre force de propositions,

c'est-à-dire qu'on propose une alternative.

Non, je ne peux pas soutiendre.

Là on le dit de manière très ferme et assurée.

Vous l'avez compris sans se justifier.

vraiment pour gérer le concurrent.

On ne se justifie pas.
